<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">The Mrs. Carter Show World Tour</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<p><b>The Mrs. Carter Show World Tour</b> was the fifth <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concert_tour" title="Concert tour">concert tour</a> by American singer <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>. Announced in February 2013 with initial dates in Europe and North America, the tour contained seven legs and 132 shows. It began in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgrade,_Serbia" title="Belgrade, Serbia">Belgrade, Serbia</a> on April 15, 2013 and concluded in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lisbon,_Portugal" title="Lisbon, Portugal">Lisbon, Portugal</a> on March 27, 2014. Its title is a reference to her marriage with American rapper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Shawn "Jay-Z" Carter</a>, who made multiple guest appearances throughout the tour.</p>
<p>The tour featured royal themes with the singer emulating different queens through her fashion for which she collaborated with numerous designers and fashion houses. The <a href="/wiki/Set_list" title="Set list">set list</a> of the shows in 2013 included songs from all four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_albums" title="Studio albums">studio albums</a> of Beyoncé's solo career. After the release of her <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9_(album)" title="Beyoncé (album)">eponymous fifth studio album</a>, the 2014 shows were changed to incorporate tracks from the album. The tour was lauded by <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a> who praised Beyoncé for her energetic performances, dancing and vocal abilities.</p>
<p>Following the announcement of the tour, all the tickets made available for the shows sold out, which prompted more dates to be added to the itinerary. The tour grossed $188.6 million in 2013 and the 2014 shows grossed $41.1 million, bringing the tour's total gross revenue to $229.7 million. This made The Mrs. Carter Show World Tour the highest-grossing female and solo tour of 2013, and one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_concert_tours#2010s" title="List of highest-grossing concert tours">highest-grossing tours of the decade</a>. Performances of numerous songs from the tour were broadcast and behind-the-scenes footage was released.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Mrs._Carter_Show_World_Tour&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jay_Z_Beyonce.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2614" data-file-width="2265" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Jay_Z_Beyonce.jpg/180px-Jay_Z_Beyonce.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Jay_Z_Beyonce.jpg/270px-Jay_Z_Beyonce.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Jay_Z_Beyonce.jpg/360px-Jay_Z_Beyonce.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jay_Z_Beyonce.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beyoncé's husband <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> (real name, Shawn Carter), served as an inspiration for the title of the tour.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During a press conference for <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVII" title="Super Bowl XLVII">Super Bowl XLVII</a> on January 31, 2013, Beyoncé revealed that she would make an announcement after her performance at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVII_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl XLVII halftime show">halftime show</a> and added that "fans should just stay tuned to see".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Beyoncé announced the tour and its name after her performance the Super Bowl XLVII halftime show on February 3. The tour's title refers to her marriage with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Shawn 'Jay-Z' Carter</a>. However, the official poster of the tour with the name written on it was leaked on the ticket's website <a href="/wiki/Live_Nation_(events_promoter)" title="Live Nation (events promoter)">Live Nation</a> prior to the official announcement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-announcement_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-announcement-2">[2]</a></sup> It shows Beyoncé wearing a Victorian golden royal top and a crown, referencing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_I" title="Queen Elizabeth I">Queen Elizabeth I</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Rosie Swash of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> described it as a "visual stamp of authority".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rossie_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-rossie-4">[4]</a></sup> Along with the tour's name, initial dates in Europe and North America were announced, and later more were added in Latin America, Australia, and New Zealand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europe_and_North_America_dates_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europe_and_North_America_dates-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the announcement of the tour's title, Beyoncé was criticized by several critics and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feminist" title="Feminist">feminists</a> alike for entitling it after her husband's name as she has been regarded as a feminist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rossie_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-rossie-4">[4]</a></sup> Questions were raised about how Beyoncé agreed to be known as a bride of another celebrity person.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> During an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Vogue_(British_magazine)" title="Vogue (British magazine)">Vogue</a></i>, Beyoncé described herself as a "modern-day feminist" and further spoke about her decision to reference her husband's name: "I feel like Mrs. Carter is who I am, but more bold and more fearless than I've ever been..... It comes from knowing my purpose and really meeting myself once I saw my child. I was like, 'OK, this is what you were born to do'. The purpose of my body became completely different."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> After the second European leg was announced on December 11, 2013, a new poster was revealed and used for the promotion of all the newly added shows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Mrs._Carter_Show_World_Tour&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:217px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:End_of_Time_Montreal_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/End_of_Time_Montreal_2013.jpg/215px-End_of_Time_Montreal_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/End_of_Time_Montreal_2013.jpg/323px-End_of_Time_Montreal_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/End_of_Time_Montreal_2013.jpg/430px-End_of_Time_Montreal_2013.jpg 2x" width="215"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:End_of_Time_Montreal_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beyoncé performing "End of Time" with the French dancing duo Les Twins and her female background dancers as pyrotechnics fell on stage.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The concert at <a href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena" title="The O2 Arena">The O<sub>2</sub> Arena</a> in London was announced on February 3, along with a short advertisement for the tour; an extended version of the clip appeared in late February. It shows Beyoncé dressed with a golden corset and a royal gown with jewels. She is seen walking into a dance hall in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slow-motion" title="Slow-motion">slow-motion</a> with several servants and a DJ, dressed as a <a href="/wiki/Jester" title="Jester">jester</a> tries to distract her. The end of the advertisement shows <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black-and-white" title="Black-and-white">black-and-white</a> snippets of behind-the-scenes footage of the video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-e_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-e-10">[10]</a></sup> Alexis L. Loinaz of <a href="/wiki/E!" title="E!">E!</a> compared her aristocratic look in the video to <a href="/wiki/Marie_Antoinette" title="Marie Antoinette">Marie Antoinette</a>, Queen Elizabeth I, and <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-e_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-e-10">[10]</a></sup> In March 2013, Beyoncé posted a new poster for the tour on her official <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> page showing her striking four different poses, wearing a blond wig, a white top and blue shorts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In May 2013, Beyoncé launched an online store for the tour in which different clothes were available for purchase.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The following month, she added a limited edition to her <a href="/wiki/Heat_(perfume)" title="Heat (perfume)">Heat</a> line of perfumes, titled Heat: The Mrs. Carter Show World Tour. Inspired by the tour, Beyoncé stated that the fragrance was meant to "give them [fans] a special remembrance of this tour and... reflect the power, passion and playfulness I put into my performances".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 24, 2013, it was announced by Beyoncé's publicist that all photographers except Beyoncé's personal photographer Frank Micelotta, were banned from the tour stating that "no photo credentials" will be present. The ban was interpreted as a reaction to the "unflattering" pictures from Beyoncé's Super Bowl XLVII halftime performance showing her "jubilant exertions", that appeared on websites such as <a href="/wiki/Gawker" title="Gawker">Gawker</a> and <a href="/wiki/BuzzFeed" title="BuzzFeed">BuzzFeed</a>. The pictures were not removed even after her publicist Yvette Noel-Schure asked the websites through an e-mail to change their articles, using "some better photos".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> On May 13, 2013, the general counsel of the <a href="/wiki/National_Press_Photographers_Association" title="National Press Photographers Association">National Press Photographers Association</a> (NPPA) Mickey H. Osterreicher, wrote a letter to Noel-Schure on behalf of 19 other organizations requesting from him to "immediately revise your guidelines to restore photo credentialing" for the rest of the tour in Europe and the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> For the tour, the singer took part in "Miss A Meal", a food-donation campaign and supported the charity <a href="/wiki/Goodwill_Industries" title="Goodwill Industries">Goodwill</a> during her tour, where fans were asked to bring food, clothes and household goods at the stops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Throughout the tour, an auction for the campaign was held by Beyoncé and her mother, <a href="/wiki/Tina_Knowles" title="Tina Knowles">Tina Knowles</a> on the website <a href="/wiki/Charitybuzz" title="Charitybuzz">Charitybuzz</a> in which the auction value was $25,000. The winner got a chance to work behind the scenes of Beyoncé's concert in Los Angeles and assist Knowles in the wardrobe department, got a VIP ticket for the concert and had a personal meeting with the singer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Eight hundred dancers auditioned to be included in Beyoncé's performance at the Super Bowl XLVII halftime show and a selected group of them, consisting only of females, were chosen for the performance as well as for the tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vibe_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-vibe-18">[18]</a></sup> French dancing duo <a href="/wiki/Les_Twins" title="Les Twins">Les Twins</a> also accompanied Beyoncé on stage performing <a href="/wiki/Street_dance" title="Street dance">street dances</a>. Three backing singers The Mamas, and an eleven-piece female band who had also supported the singer during her previous tours performed during the concerts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-book_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-book-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Two stages were used during the performances: a main stage where the singer performed throughout most of the concert and a <a href="/wiki/B-stage" title="B-stage">B-stage</a> closer to the audience where she was transferred with a rope, flying over the crowd midway through the set, performing three songs there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vibe_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-vibe-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spy_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-spy-21">[21]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Set_list" title="Set list">set list</a> of the 2013 portion of the tour included approximately twenty five songs from Beyoncé's four solo studio albums: <i><a href="/wiki/Dangerously_in_Love" title="Dangerously in Love">Dangerously in Love</a></i> (2003), <i><a href="/wiki/B%27Day_(Beyonc%C3%A9_album)" title="B'Day (Beyoncé album)">B'Day</a></i> (2006), <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am..._Sasha_Fierce" title="I Am... Sasha Fierce">I Am... Sasha Fierce</a></i> (2008), and <i><a href="/wiki/4_(Beyonc%C3%A9_album)" title="4 (Beyoncé album)">4</a></i> (2011). The majority of the songs originated from <i>4</i> – seven songs were performed from that album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hollywood_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-hollywood-22">[22]</a></sup> Many of the tracks performed contained different choreographies and arrangements compared to the previous performances by the singer; several of them were intertwined with other artists' material.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraf_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-telegraf-23">[23]</a></sup> For the 2014 shows many of the previously performed songs were removed and eight new songs from Beyoncé's fifth <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9_(album)" title="Beyoncé (album)">self-titled studio album</a> were added to the concert's set list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-biggerisbetter_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-biggerisbetter-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion">Fashion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Mrs._Carter_Show_World_Tour&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Fashion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beyonce_Freakum_Dress_Live.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Beyonce_Freakum_Dress_Live.jpg/220px-Beyonce_Freakum_Dress_Live.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Beyonce_Freakum_Dress_Live.jpg/330px-Beyonce_Freakum_Dress_Live.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Beyonce_Freakum_Dress_Live.jpg/440px-Beyonce_Freakum_Dress_Live.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beyonce_Freakum_Dress_Live.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beyoncé and her female dancers performing "Freakum Dress" during a concert. For the performance of the song they wore long dresses in different colours.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For the 2013 shows, Beyoncé worked with multiple designers for the tour's costumes including <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Pucci" title="Emilio Pucci">Emilio Pucci</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Riccardo_Tisci" title="Riccardo Tisci">Riccardo Tisci</a> from <a href="/wiki/Givenchy" title="Givenchy">Givenchy</a>, The Blonds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-beyonce.com_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-beyonce.com-26">[26]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julien_MacDonald" title="Julien MacDonald">Julien MacDonald</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Almassi_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Almassi-27">[27]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dean_and_Dan_Caten" title="Dean and Dan Caten">Dean and Dan Caten</a> (DSQUARED<sup>2</sup>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvstyle_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvstyle-28">[28]</a></sup> creative director Tamara Ralph of <a href="/wiki/Ralph_%26_Russo" title="Ralph &amp; Russo">Ralph &amp; Russo</a> who was personally requested by the singer to design an outfit,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwd_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-wwd-29">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Koma" title="David Koma">David Koma</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alon_Livne" title="Alon Livne">Alon Livne</a>, Vrettos Vrettakos<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvstyle_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtvstyle-28">[28]</a></sup> designers from <a href="/wiki/Kenzo_(brand)" title="Kenzo (brand)">Kenzo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gucci" title="Gucci">Gucci</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Cavalli" title="Roberto Cavalli">Roberto Cavalli</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> and Dennis Kolpodinos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> For the performance at the 2013 Made in America, Beyoncé wore a new costume designed by Timothy White, accomponied with shoes made by Reed Krakoff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The outfit designed by DSQUARED<sup>2</sup> was from their spring/summer 2013 collection at the <i>Glamazon</i> catwalk show and was inspired by models of the '90s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-duo_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-duo-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Several costumes were also designed by Emilio Pucci's Peter Dundas who described them as a "modern take on glamour", taking them from his fall/winter 2013 collection. He focused on the singer being able to perform the choreography during her performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Weitzman" title="Stuart Weitzman">Stuart Weitzman</a> designed the shoes for Beyoncé, her back-up dancers and band collaborating with stylists Ty Hunter, Raquel Smith, and Beyoncé's mother <a href="/wiki/Tina_Knowles" title="Tina Knowles">Tina Knowles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usashoes_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-usashoes-39">[39]</a></sup> Weitzman created them in different colors with military elements. Beyoncé wanted Weitzman to focus on her being able to dance wearing the shoes without noticing they were on her feet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> One of Beyoncé's costumes which was worn during the first concerts was a gold bodysuit designed by The Blonds embellished with golden breasts complete with a nipple detail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billfashion_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-billfashion-41">[41]</a></sup> The costume was a collaboration between the group, Beyoncé, Knowles, and Hunter. It was hand embroidered in 600 hours with approximately 30,000 Swarovski crystals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fashionista_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-fashionista-42">[42]</a></sup> According to The Blonds, it was meant to give the illusion of being covered in crystallized honey and reflect Beyoncé's personality for the tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fashionista_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-fashionista-42">[42]</a></sup> They were inspired by Beyoncé's songs of female empowerment<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billfashion_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-billfashion-41">[41]</a></sup> and female nudes painted by <a href="/wiki/Tamara_de_Lempicka" title="Tamara de Lempicka">Tamara de Lempicka</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-instyle_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-instyle-43">[43]</a></sup> The costume received wide media and fan attention and divided critics' opinions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/InStyle" title="InStyle">InStyle</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Meghan Blalock described the costume as the "most scandalous" that the singer has worn in her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-instyle_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-instyle-43">[43]</a></sup> For the 2014 shows, the singer wore numerous new designs collaborating again with DSQUARED<sup>2</sup>, Givenchy, Pucci and Weitzman as well as with new designers such as <a href="/wiki/Tom_Ford" title="Tom Ford">Tom Ford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Versace" title="Versace">Versace</a> and Karen Langley.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-out_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-out-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grown_Woman_2013_Montreal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Grown_Woman_2013_Montreal.jpg/220px-Grown_Woman_2013_Montreal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Grown_Woman_2013_Montreal.jpg/330px-Grown_Woman_2013_Montreal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Grown_Woman_2013_Montreal.jpg/440px-Grown_Woman_2013_Montreal.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grown_Woman_2013_Montreal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beyoncé performing "Grown Woman" with her female background dancers, wearing animal printed dresses. The projection behind them showed African-inspired video projection.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beyoncé's makeup for the tour focused on trying to emulate cosmic stars with the underlying themes based on the <a href="/wiki/Stratosphere" title="Stratosphere">stratosphere</a>. Other references used as inspiration for the makeup included: <a href="/wiki/Film_noir" title="Film noir">film noir</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_in_the_1960s" title="London in the 1960s">60's London</a>, cyber beauty, cosmic constellations, and <a href="/wiki/Cat" title="Cat">felines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The tourbook for The Mrs. Carter Show was meant to artistically illustrate all the different visual aspects of the tour through multi-media collage and <a href="/wiki/Photo_manipulation" title="Photo manipulation">image manipulation</a>. By using collage, Beyoncé's team created images inspired by the singer and her songs and image manipulation was explored, with photos being <a href="/wiki/Solarisation" title="Solarisation">solarized</a>, <a href="/wiki/Layers_(digital_image_editing)" title="Layers (digital image editing)">layered</a> and stacked. With the tourbook, fans had an opportunity to "bring a part of the tour home with them", as Beyoncé's team stated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> A dress created by Amato Haute Couture's Furne One which was worn by Beyoncé for the tour book was originally designed and worn by Estonian singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Kerli" title="Kerli">Kerli</a> during her <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Utopia_(EP)" title="Utopia (EP)">Utopia</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a> photoshoot who praised the look after seeing it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>The concert included several costume changes during which video interludes were projected on the screen during the singer's absence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hollywood_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-hollywood-22">[22]</a></sup> An <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/18th_Century_France" title="18th Century France">18th Century France</a> influence was found in the white-powder makeup and the opening costume as well as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_XVI" title="Louis XVI">Louis XVI</a> theme throughout the show with oversized wigs and bustiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spy_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-spy-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardreview_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardreview-52">[52]</a></sup> The dresses and looks were also noted to channel queens Marie Antionette, <a href="/wiki/Cleopatra" title="Cleopatra">Cleopatra</a>, and Elizabeth I by several critics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <a href="/wiki/Kitty_Empire" title="Kitty Empire">Kitty Empire</a> described the concert as a <a href="/wiki/Fashion" title="Fashion">fashion</a> show with a regal, <i><a href="/wiki/Dangerous_Liaisons" title="Dangerous Liaisons">Dangerous Liaisons</a></i> theme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empire_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-empire-54">[54]</a></sup> Jocelyn Vena of MTV News described the costumes as "Eye-catching... dazzling... [and] provocative".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Rosa Silverman of <i>The Daily Telegraph</i> commented that Beyoncé was "mesmerizing the crowds with her showstopping outfits... she took to the stage in a series of racy costumes that made no attempt to hide her famous curves."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Erika Ramirez of <i>Billboard</i> commented that most of Beyoncé's "stunning" costumes were dazzled with sequins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Concert_synopsis">Concert synopsis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Mrs._Carter_Show_World_Tour&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Concert synopsis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_shows">2013 shows</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Mrs._Carter_Show_World_Tour&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2013 shows">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:368px;max-width:368px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Get_Me_Bodied_Beyonce_2013.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Get_Me_Bodied_Beyonce_2013.jpg/180px-Get_Me_Bodied_Beyonce_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Get_Me_Bodied_Beyonce_2013.jpg/270px-Get_Me_Bodied_Beyonce_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Get_Me_Bodied_Beyonce_2013.jpg/360px-Get_Me_Bodied_Beyonce_2013.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg/180px-Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg/270px-Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg/360px-Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Immediately after Beyoncé finished with the performance of "Get Me Bodied" with her background dancers, (<i>left</i>) they went in front of a holographic background continuing with "Baby Boy" (<i>right</i>).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The concert opened with a pre-recorded video montage showing black and white footage of <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">gothic architecture</a> as well as dancers dressed in white, marching across a stage length screen, preparing to crown Beyoncé who was dressed as a queen. The montage continued as female dancers wearing hoop-skirt cages and masks started appearing on stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ok_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-ok-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billlaunch_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-billlaunch-59">[59]</a></sup> The video wall raised afterwards and a brief pyrotechnics display began as Beyoncé appeared onstage standing for several seconds prior to the performance of "<a href="/wiki/Run_the_World_(Girls)" title="Run the World (Girls)">Run the World (Girls)</a>" preceded by an extended timpani interlude.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardreview_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-guardreview-52">[52]</a></sup> She sang the song while performing a choreography which included a routine of faux kicking her male dancers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spy_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-spy-21">[21]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/End_of_Time_(song)" title="End of Time (song)">End of Time</a>" followed with Beyoncé dancing as fireworks were also displayed on stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flawed_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-flawed-60">[60]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Flaws_and_All" title="Flaws and All">Flaws and All</a>" was performed as the third song on the set list with Beyoncé dedicating it to her fan group, the BeyHive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billlaunch_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-billlaunch-59">[59]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/If_I_Were_a_Boy" title="If I Were a Boy">If I Were a Boy</a>" was <a href="/wiki/Mashup_(music)" title="Mashup (music)">mashed</a> with <a href="/wiki/The_Verve" title="The Verve">The Verve</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Bitter_Sweet_Symphony" title="Bitter Sweet Symphony">Bitter Sweet Symphony</a>" taking the latter's string motif and incorporating several lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimesrev_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimesrev-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nmelist_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-nmelist-62">[62]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Get_Me_Bodied" title="Get Me Bodied">Get Me Bodied</a>" saw Beyoncé interacting with the audience through <a href="/wiki/Call_and_response" title="Call and response">call and response</a>, asking them to repeat "Hey, Mrs. Carter".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billlaunch_59-2"><a href="#cite_note-billlaunch-59">[59]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Baby_Boy_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Baby Boy (Beyoncé song)">Baby Boy</a>" was performed against a <a href="/wiki/Holography" title="Holography">holographic background</a> as Beyoncé and several female dancers performed synchronised moves in front of the screen which flashed realistic images of more identical dancers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimesrev_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-latimesrev-61">[61]</a></sup> The singer concluded the song with a <a href="/wiki/Dutty_Wine" title="Dutty Wine">Dutty Wine</a> dance at the end of the performance, before immediately continuing with "<a href="/wiki/Diva_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Diva (Beyoncé song)">Diva</a>" which was set to the <a href="/wiki/Groove_(music)" title="Groove (music)">groove</a> of "<a href="/wiki/Clique_(song)" title="Clique (song)">Clique</a>". "<a href="/wiki/Naughty_Girl_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Naughty Girl (Beyoncé song)">Naughty Girl</a>" was later performed into a neon strip-lit with a snippet of <a href="/wiki/Donna_Summer" title="Donna Summer">Donna Summer</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Love_to_Love_You_Baby_(song)" title="Love to Love You Baby (song)">Love to Love You Baby</a>" interpolated within it. Beyoncé also performed a seductive dance in front of an open fire display onstage. "<a href="/wiki/Party_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Party (Beyoncé song)">Party</a>" was performed after with a prominent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_showgirl" title="Las Vegas showgirl">Las Vegas showgirl</a> theme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wass_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-wass-63">[63]</a></sup> For "<a href="/wiki/Freakum_Dress" title="Freakum Dress">Freakum Dress</a>" two ballerinas appeared on stage and performed a choreography along with a video projection on the screen. Beyoncé later appeared in a deep-plunging, thigh-high split long red dress performing the song along with her dancers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billlaunch_59-3"><a href="#cite_note-billlaunch-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:368px;max-width:368px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beyonce_1%2B1_live_(2).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Beyonce_1%2B1_live_%282%29.jpg/180px-Beyonce_1%2B1_live_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Beyonce_1%2B1_live_%282%29.jpg/270px-Beyonce_1%2B1_live_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Beyonce_1%2B1_live_%282%29.jpg/360px-Beyonce_1%2B1_live_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beyonce_B-Stage_Montreal_2013.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Beyonce_B-Stage_Montreal_2013.jpg/180px-Beyonce_B-Stage_Montreal_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Beyonce_B-Stage_Montreal_2013.jpg/270px-Beyonce_B-Stage_Montreal_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Beyonce_B-Stage_Montreal_2013.jpg/360px-Beyonce_B-Stage_Montreal_2013.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Beyoncé performing "1+1" seated on a piano. After the performance of the song, she flew with a wire to a B-stage, closer to the people in the crowd (<i>right</i>).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For "<a href="/wiki/I_Care_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="I Care (Beyoncé song)">I Care</a>" the singer was dressed in a black leather fedora, seated on a bar stool.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nmelist_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-nmelist-62">[62]</a></sup> Beyoncé sang "<a href="/wiki/I_Miss_You_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="I Miss You (Beyoncé song)">I Miss You</a>" while shadow dancing was illustrated on the screen behind her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OMH_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-OMH-64">[64]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Schoolin%27_Life" title="Schoolin' Life">Schoolin' Life</a>" was performed with a <a href="/wiki/Laser_lighting_display" title="Laser lighting display">light show</a> complete with '80s <a href="/wiki/Neon_lighting" title="Neon lighting">neon lights</a> while she performed a dance routine with her dancers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billlaunch_59-4"><a href="#cite_note-billlaunch-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wass_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-wass-63">[63]</a></sup> An uptempo version of "<a href="/wiki/Why_Don%27t_You_Love_Me_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Why Don't You Love Me (Beyoncé song)">Why Don't You Love Me</a>" with a choreography by Beyoncé and <a href="/wiki/Les_Twins" title="Les Twins">Les Twins</a> was preceded by a video projection showing a vintage montage of her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empire_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-empire-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wass_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-wass-63">[63]</a></sup> The singer performed the song with a call and response interaction between her and the audience dressed in a 1920s fringed dress. The performance of "1+1" saw Beyoncé in a blue cat-suit kneeling and laying atop a grand piano.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billlaunch_59-5"><a href="#cite_note-billlaunch-59">[59]</a></sup> During the end of "1+1", she was transformed from the main stage to the B-stage, located closer to the crowd with a wire through a cloud of glitter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nmelist_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-nmelist-62">[62]</a></sup> "Irreplaceable" was performed after that with an audience sing-along.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billlaunch_59-6"><a href="#cite_note-billlaunch-59">[59]</a></sup> "Love on Top" and an abbreviated version of <a href="/wiki/Destiny%27s_Child" title="Destiny's Child">Destiny's Child</a>'s "Survivor" followed; Beyoncé dedicated the latter song to the members of the aforementioned girl group, <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Rowland" title="Kelly Rowland">Kelly Rowland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Williams_(singer)" title="Michelle Williams (singer)">Michelle Williams</a>. Beyoncé was taken back to the main stage being transferred with the same wire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spy_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-spy-21">[21]</a></sup> "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crazy_in_Love_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Crazy in Love (Beyoncé song)">Crazy in Love</a>" was the first song performed on the main stage with a new brassy arrangement, different from Beyoncé's other live performances of the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wass_63-3"><a href="#cite_note-wass-63">[63]</a></sup> During "<a href="/wiki/Single_Ladies_(Put_a_Ring_on_It)" title="Single Ladies (Put a Ring on It)">Single Ladies (Put a Ring on It)</a>", she integrated a snippet from the song "<a href="/wiki/The_Jeffersons#Theme_song" title="The Jeffersons">Movin' on Up</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billlaunch_59-7"><a href="#cite_note-billlaunch-59">[59]</a></sup> Images of pyramids, animated lions and elephants and a portrait of the singer wearing a <a href="/wiki/Nefertiti" title="Nefertiti">Nefertiti</a>-style crown were displayed on the screen before the performance of "Grown Woman", keeping in line with the song's African influence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimesrev_61-2"><a href="#cite_note-latimesrev-61">[61]</a></sup> During the performance, the singer and her dancers wore African-inspired costumes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spy_21-4"><a href="#cite_note-spy-21">[21]</a></sup> A montage was shown with the song "<a href="/wiki/I_Was_Here_(song)" title="I Was Here (song)">I Was Here</a>" being played in the background showing footage of the singer with <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, taking part in charity work, during a vacation with Jay-Z and excerpts of her 2013 performance at the Super Bowl.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OMH_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-OMH-64">[64]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a> performance of the opening lines of "<a href="/wiki/I_Will_Always_Love_You#Beyonc.C3.A9_Knowles_version" title="I Will Always Love You">I Will Always Love You</a>" preceded "Halo" as the closing song of the concert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spy_21-5"><a href="#cite_note-spy-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billlaunch_59-8"><a href="#cite_note-billlaunch-59">[59]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Green_Light_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Green Light (Beyoncé song)">Green Light</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Suga_Mama" title="Suga Mama">Suga Mama</a>" were used for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encore_(concert)" title="Encore (concert)">encore</a> of the concert at numerous stops.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_shows">2014 shows</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Mrs._Carter_Show_World_Tour&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2014 shows">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The performances of the songs that had already been performed during the 2013 shows remained the same; however some of them were shortened and mixed together. Many new songs from the singer's fifth album were added to the set list with a specific staging and theme. The projections shown on the stage followed the concept behind the singer's visual album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-biggerisbetter_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-biggerisbetter-24">[24]</a></sup> The performance of "<a href="/wiki/Flawless_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Flawless (Beyoncé song)">Flawless</a>", the second song on the set, opened with the words from <a href="/wiki/Chimamanda_Ngozi_Adichie" title="Chimamanda Ngozi Adichie">Chimamanda Ngozi Adichie</a>'s <a href="/wiki/TED_(conference)" title="TED (conference)">TED</a> talk projected with big letters on the screen and later Beyoncé performed a choreography with her female dancers similarly to the song's music video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014tel_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-2014tel-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv2014_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtv2014-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ind_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-ind-67">[67]</a></sup> A performance of "Yoncé" followed with a new choreography with her dancers. "<a href="/wiki/Blow_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Blow (Beyoncé song)">Blow</a>" was merged with "Naughty Girl" (2003) and featured a <a href="/wiki/Burlesque" title="Burlesque">burlesque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a>-era theme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pacman_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-pacman-68">[68]</a></sup> During the end of the performance a projection of <a href="/wiki/Pac-Man_(character)" title="Pac-Man (character)">Pac-Man</a>, the character of the <a href="/wiki/Pac-Man" title="Pac-Man">game with the same name</a>, eating cherries was projected on an LED screen onstage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pacman_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-pacman-68">[68]</a></sup> "Partition" was performed in a similar fashion to its music video with Beyoncé appearing with a silhouette, dancing on a couch in front of a purple light.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-biggerisbetter_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-biggerisbetter-24">[24]</a></sup> For "<a href="/wiki/Drunk_in_Love" title="Drunk in Love">Drunk in Love</a>", the singer performed a choreographed chair dance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv2014_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtv2014-66">[66]</a></sup> During "<a href="/wiki/Haunted_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Haunted (Beyoncé song)">Haunted</a>", strobing lights and dancers were present on stage. "Heaven" and "<a href="/wiki/XO_(song)" title="XO (song)">XO</a>" were performed as the concert's last songs along with "Halo".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-biggerisbetter_24-3"><a href="#cite_note-biggerisbetter-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Mrs._Carter_Show_World_Tour&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Naughty_Girl_Beyonce_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Naughty_Girl_Beyonce_2013.jpg/220px-Naughty_Girl_Beyonce_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Naughty_Girl_Beyonce_2013.jpg/330px-Naughty_Girl_Beyonce_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Naughty_Girl_Beyonce_2013.jpg/440px-Naughty_Girl_Beyonce_2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Naughty_Girl_Beyonce_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beyoncé performing "Naughty Girl" with onstage pyrotechnics.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mike Wass from the website <a href="/wiki/Idolator_(website)" title="Idolator (website)">Idolator</a> called the show a "concert extravaganza in the style of <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> or <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>" praising the fact that the singer made a progress in the production values compared with her previous performances, mostly due to the expensive and high-quality visual projections which "create atmosphere and add another layer to the production".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wass_63-4"><a href="#cite_note-wass-63">[63]</a></sup> He further praised the singer's "extraordinary talent" during the performances hailing her as "the greatest entertainer of her generation" after seeing the show which showcased "an icon at top of her game".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wass_63-5"><a href="#cite_note-wass-63">[63]</a></sup> Tiffany Poole from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oklahoman" title="The Oklahoman">The Oklahoman</a></i> praised the fashion, video backdrops and "some of the most impersonated dance moves on YouTube" concluding, "To say that Beyoncé puts on a good show would be grossly understated."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ok_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-ok-58">[58]</a></sup> <i>Billboard</i> writer Gail Mitchell hailed the concert as a "musical and visual extravaganza" complete with a kaleidoscope of colorful imagery and dancing, which according to him enhanced the music complete with the singer's strong vocals, rather than overshadowing it. He concluded that the tour claimed "the multi-talented artist's intent to join the rarefied ranks of ultimate entertainer".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billlaunch_59-9"><a href="#cite_note-billlaunch-59">[59]</a></sup> Nick Hasted of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> wrote that the tour followed the stadium trends containing "big-budget movie clips and <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway musical</a> dance moves, with platoons of backing singers and dancers acting as extras" further hailing it as a "<a href="/wiki/Cecil_B._DeMille" title="Cecil B. DeMille">Cecil B. DeMille</a> spectacle". He finished his reviews by concluding, "what makes this show's largely enervating juggernaut breathe is Beyoncé's tireless physical effort. She has created a literal body of work".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theindependent_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-theindependent-69">[69]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Petridis" title="Alexis Petridis">Alexis Petridis</a> of <i>The Guardian</i> who compared the singer's performance with <a href="/wiki/Tina_Turner" title="Tina Turner">Tina Turner</a> praised the show's "bombastic" opening and wrote that "there's something powerful and relentless" about it. He concluded "while onstage Beyoncé feels weirdly unassailable".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardreview_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-guardreview-52">[52]</a></sup> Mikael Wood of <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> noted, "What left the deepest impression was something far more elemental: Beyoncé's ability to make self-aggrandizement seem like an expression of humility... [Her] ambition seemed in proportion with her fans' expectations; she came by the sense of scale honestly."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimesrev_61-3"><a href="#cite_note-latimesrev-61">[61]</a></sup> <i>The Observer</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Kitty Empire highlighted the art direction of the show as "nothing short of breathtaking, making awesome and repeated use of silhouette, of great white blocks of video screens, of live dancers interacting with video". She praised the singer's "fierce" tireless dancing and concluded, "But for all the hauteur here, in couture and bearing, Beyoncé delivers genuine warmth at close range."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empire_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-empire-54">[54]</a></sup> Bernadette McNulty from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> found "air of an ancient goddess worship ceremony... [and] of an expensive revue show" in the concert. Although she felt that the choreographies often outshined the music, McNulty concluded: "Yet Beyonce was never less than compelling to watch, and often blistering in her vocal attack".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraf_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-telegraf-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Philip Matusavage of <a href="/wiki/MusicOMH" title="MusicOMH">musicOMH</a> praised Beyoncé's abilities to perform live, calling her "insanely talented" and considered the performance at the B-stage a show highlight; however he commented that the production values of the show, consisting solely of a video screen were "relatively low-key" compared to other pop arena concerts. Matusavage further criticized the repetition of the songs and dance routines which had been previously performed during the singer's other concerts as the tour's "most notable problem".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OMH_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-OMH-64">[64]</a></sup> Shirley Halperin of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> felt that the singer "tore through her... set with the ferocity of a grown woman who has something to prove" and felt that she tried "her damnedest to win the crowd over with an equal dose of sex appeal and good old-fashioned hyping" further showcasing "unequaled showmanship and those killer vocals" which placed her at the top of R&amp;B music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hollywood_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-hollywood-22">[22]</a></sup> However Halperin criticized the show's set list mainly due to the majority of the songs from the album <i>4</i>, writing, "Bey sounded terrific on all, of course, but with a... ready-to-party audience angling to groove in the aisles, rather than sway with their hands to the heavens, overall it missed the mark."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hollywood_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-hollywood-22">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Digital_Spy" title="Digital Spy">Digital Spy</a>'s Robert Copsey praised the high-energy nature of the show with vigorous dancing and "blistering" pace but felt that there was a lack of hits performed in the show's first half.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spy_21-6"><a href="#cite_note-spy-21">[21]</a></sup> <i>NME</i> editor Emily Mackay echoed his statements giving a mixed review for the tour, further criticizing the lack of hits in the set list and adding that only a "paucity of material" was incorporated in the set. She further dismissed the placement of interlude films in the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> A negative review came from <i><a href="/wiki/San_Jose_Mercury_News" title="San Jose Mercury News">San Jose Mercury News</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span> Jim Harrington who called the tour "flawed", criticized its set list consisting of "plenty of filler[s]" and the many dissipating costume changes she went through for the show. He further noted that the singer looked and sounded well but blamed the way the show and the production were choreographed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flawed_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-flawed-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beyonce_Crazy_in_love_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Beyonce_Crazy_in_love_2013.jpg/220px-Beyonce_Crazy_in_love_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Beyonce_Crazy_in_love_2013.jpg/330px-Beyonce_Crazy_in_love_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Beyonce_Crazy_in_love_2013.jpg/440px-Beyonce_Crazy_in_love_2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beyonce_Crazy_in_love_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beyoncé and her background dancers performing a choreography during "Crazy in Love"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The revamped show in 2014 received acclaim by critics. Isabel Mohan from <i>The Daily Telegraph</i> acclaimed the revamped show praising the singer's sex appeal and noted that although the set included many new songs, the singer "remained strikingly composed and confident throughout a show which proved her talent, charisma and awe-inspiring thighs".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014tel_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-2014tel-65">[65]</a></sup> Sidney Madden who praised the upgraded set list further commended the show's fashion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv2014_66-2"><a href="#cite_note-mtv2014-66">[66]</a></sup> Digital Spy's Robert Copsey felt that the show's set list was better than the original one describing the tour as "wall-to-wall amazing Beyoncé". He concluded in his review, "The relentless pace, ever-changing visuals and sheer amount of songs crammed into the set is a lot to take in, let alone the fact that Beyoncé delivers the entire thing with power yet impeccable ease. When it comes to putting on a show of this calibre, these days she's really only competing with herself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-biggerisbetter_24-4"><a href="#cite_note-biggerisbetter-24">[24]</a></sup> <i>The Observer</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Kitty Empire praised the singer's ranuchiness during the tour different from the other performers and concluded by writing, "There is no question as to Beyoncé's own powers. She can stop and start her all-female band... with a click of her fingers, and keep climbing octaves until you think her lungs are about to jump out of her chest. She sings (with a range that only gets wider and deeper with every tour) and dances (flawlessly) for more than one and a half hours."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pacman_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-pacman-68">[68]</a></sup> David Pollock of <i>The Independent</i> felt that, "this near two-hour epic is a ferocious distillation of musical styles old and new and a stunning declaration of intent that Knowles intends to be recognised as the defining pop artist of her era. It was, at the very least, one of the hardest working shows likely to be witnessed on a stage this year, and with barely a drop of minutely-choreographed sweat to be seen."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ind_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-ind-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tour received a nomination in the category for Choice Summer Tour at the 2013 Teen Choice Summer Tour losing to <a href="/wiki/One_Direction" title="One Direction">One Direction</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Take_Me_Home_Tour_(One_Direction)" title="Take Me Home Tour (One Direction)">Take Me Home Tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> It was also nominated for Concert Marketing &amp; Promotion Award and Eventful Fans' Choice Award at the 2013 Billboard Music Awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-touring_award13_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-touring_award13-72">[72]</a></sup> The tour is nominated in the category for Best Tour at the 2014 Billboard Mid-Year Music Awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Mrs._Carter_Show_World_Tour&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Following the general on-sale of tickets, tour stops in several cities across America sold out in minutes after being announced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Due to the high demand, one extra show was added in Amsterdam, one extra show in Antwerp, two extra shows in London and a third date in Manchester. In North America, extra dates were added in Washington, D.C. Los Angeles and New York City. Phone firm <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/O2_(United_Kingdom)" title="O2 (United Kingdom)">O2</a>, which was behind the pre-sale of the UK shows, said it could have sold out London's O<sub>2</sub> Arena 150 times with the number of website hits with a spokesman noting the "unprecedented level of demand from O2 customers looking to buy tickets".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Following the frenzied rush for tickets during the general sale, the UK tour had completely sold out within three minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Tickets for <a href="/wiki/Rock_in_Rio" title="Rock in Rio">Rock in Rio</a> became available for general sale on April 4, 2013 and within two hours, the first day of the festival, in which Beyoncé was headlining, had sold out all 65,000 tickets. 20,000 tickets had already sold out from the pre-sale a few months before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> On July 7, 2013, Beyoncé's performance at the Essence Music Festival broke the attendance record with over 70,000 people in attendance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> On June 24, 2013, a second wave of tour dates were announced via Beyoncé's official website. Included in this was a second US leg as well as a Latin American leg, containing multiple stadium dates in Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> It was revealed that Beyoncé set the record for the highest number of concert attendees in Brazil for the year 2013, with more than 230,000 fans attending her 5 shows in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mrs_Carter_Show_World_Tour_poster_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="389" data-file-width="300" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ef/Mrs_Carter_Show_World_Tour_poster_2.jpg/220px-Mrs_Carter_Show_World_Tour_poster_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/ef/Mrs_Carter_Show_World_Tour_poster_2.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mrs_Carter_Show_World_Tour_poster_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A second promotional poster for the tour was used to promote the 2014 shows in Europe.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On July 7, 2013, the Australasia leg of the tour was announced, with dates set for shows in Australia and New Zealand, where Beyoncé held a concert for the first time in her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-australasia_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-australasia-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Fan club tickets for the October 18, 2013 show in Auckland, New Zealand sold out in 3 minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The general sale for the New Zealand shows became available to the public on July 19, 2013 and within 15 minutes all allocations of tickets were sold out for the three shows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> A fourth and final Auckland show was then added. Promoter Live Nation confirmed The Mrs. Carter Show World Tour was officially the fastest selling tour of all time at Vector Arena.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> It also became the concert with the highest attendance at Vector Arena by a solo artist, with 44,596 tickets sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Beyoncé's two shows at the <a href="/wiki/Perth_Arena" title="Perth Arena">Perth Arena</a> went on to hold the number one and two spots for highest attendance in a single show, dethroning previous record holder <a href="/wiki/Pink_(singer)" title="Pink (singer)">Pink</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> It was then announced that Beyoncé's Australasian leg of the tour was one of the most successful tours in the continent from any artist, playing for more than 220,000 fans and earning 40 million <a href="/wiki/Australian_dollar" title="Australian dollar">Australian dollars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 11, 2013, a second European leg through 2014 was announced bringing the total number of shows to 132, thus becoming Beyoncé's longest running tour to date. Similar to the first European leg, a frenzied rush for tickets, further enhanced by the release of the singer's <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9_(album)" title="Beyoncé (album)">self-titled fifth studio album</a> three days before ticket sales began, resulted in extra dates being added for all United Kingdom shows, Dublin, Cologne, Amsterdam and Antwerp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> For the second European leg, Beyoncé had beaten the record she herself had set earlier in the year, by selling 40,000 tickets in under one hour for the two 2014 concerts at Antwerp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Pollstar" title="Pollstar">Pollstar</a></i> ranked The Mrs. Carter Show at number 2 on its year-end chart of the top twenty grossing worldwide tours with a gross of $188.6 million from the 2013 shows. Tickets were sold with an average gross of $2,449,248 per city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pollstar3012_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-pollstar3012-91">[91]</a></sup> In April 2014, <i>Billboard</i> reported that Beyoncé's 2014 European shows grossed $41.1 million and played for an audience of 384,730.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014_box_office_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-2014_box_office-92">[92]</a></sup> This brought The Mrs. Carter Show World Tour's total gross to $229.7 million when combined with the 107 shows performed in 2013, and the total attendance to 2,082,848, averaging 15,779 attendance and $1.74 million gross per night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The tour is Beyoncé's highest grossing to date before being surpassed by <a href="/wiki/The_Formation_World_Tour" title="The Formation World Tour">The Formation World Tour</a> which grossed over $256 milion, and one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_concert_tours#2010s" title="List of highest-grossing concert tours">highest grossing tours of the decade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcasts_and_recordings">Broadcasts and recordings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Mrs._Carter_Show_World_Tour&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Broadcasts and recordings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beyonce_Party_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Beyonce_Party_2013.jpg/210px-Beyonce_Party_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Beyonce_Party_2013.jpg/315px-Beyonce_Party_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Beyonce_Party_2013.jpg/420px-Beyonce_Party_2013.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beyonce_Party_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beyoncé performing "Party" which featured a Las Vegas showgirl theme</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Professional footage from the tour was officially released on April 22, 2013 through Beyoncé's <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> channel and website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> It showed the opening moments of the show and performances of "Run the World (Girls)", "Love on Top" and "Halo" during the first concerts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> A series of eight behind-the-scenes footage of the rehearsals and preparations for the tour were released on Beyoncé's website on May 21, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> During "The Sound of Change Live" charity concert held at Twickenham Stadium in London on June 1, 2013, various clips and performances were broadcast worldwide to over 150 countries which were believed to have reached over 1 billion people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>A thirty-second trailer for the tour was released on June 24, 2013 containing live vocals of Beyoncé's "Get Me Bodied" and a <a href="/wiki/Dubstep" title="Dubstep">dubstep</a> audio mix. It showed footage from the tour's commercial and multiple snippets of live performances from the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-datesD_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-datesD-99">[99]</a></sup> On August 29, 2013, Beyoncé posted a video titled "Bey Good" on her official website showing scenes of her with fans backstage and during the concerts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> During Beyoncé's performance at the Made in America Festival, the two opening songs—"Run the World (Girls)" and "End of Time"—were streamed live via YouTube.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Beyoncé's performance at Rock in Rio was broadcast in its entirety, and also streamed via YouTube.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> On August 22, 2013, Beyoncé released a black-and-white promotional retro video for the tour dates in Brazil. It was set to <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">Frank Sinatra</a>'s version of the song "<a href="/wiki/The_Girl_from_Ipanema" title="The Girl from Ipanema">The Girl from Ipanema</a>". The video featured the singer in a bikini swimming in the water, writing Brazil in the sand and relaxing on a hammock as well as various shots of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2014, a new promotional video was released midway through the second European leg and first leg of the 2014 tour. This was the first venture of the tour to include new performances and songs from Beyoncé's recently released self-titled fifth studio album. The video showed professional clips from some new performances and also featured a variety of backstage activity from the revamped tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> A video titled "Goodbye to The Mrs. Carter Show World Tour" was uploaded by the singer on her official YouTube channel on March 27, 2014 showing portions of live performances from the final leg of the tour, behind the scenes moments and visits to cities as "XO" was played in the background.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> In June 2014 it was announced that <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> would air <i>Beyonce: X10</i>, a 10-episode series of four-minute segments of concert performances debuting weekly before new episodes of <i><a href="/wiki/True_Blood" title="True Blood">True Blood</a></i> starting June 29. The performances were captured in various cities during the tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> They are included on a bonus disc in the platinum edition release of Beyoncé's <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9_(album)" title="Beyoncé (album)">2013 self-titled album</a>, which was released on November 24, 2014.</p>

<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;">
<div class="NavHead" style="background:transparent;text-align:center;background: #FFE6FF; font-size: 100%; width: 90%;">Notes </div>
<div class="NavContent" style="background:transparent;text-align:left;text-align: left; font-size: 100%; width: 90%;">
<ul>
<li>"Grown Woman" was performed for the first time in Paris on April 24, 2013 and was later permanently included to the set list for all future stops, until the second North American leg where the song was only performed in select cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li>"<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standing_on_the_Sun_(song)" title="Standing on the Sun (song)">Standing on the Sun</a>" was performed live for the first and only time in Antwerp on May 31, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></li>
<li>During The Sound of Change Live charity concert held at Twickenham Stadium in London on June 1, 2013, Beyoncé was accompanied by an 8-piece string section. She was joined by husband <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> on stage whilst performing "Crazy in Love". The show lasted for 45 minutes and contained unique, one-time only costumes designed by Gucci for the special event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></li>
<li>"Bow Down" was performed for the first time during the concert in Beyoncé's hometown of Houston, Texas on July 15, 2013. During the beginning of the performance, images of Beyonce's dancers as children with the words "Bow Down" flashed across the screen appeared as sound bites of <a href="/wiki/Blind_item" title="Blind item">gossip reports</a> were heard in the background. Beyoncé addressed many rumors surrounding her throughout her career including faking her pregnancy with daughter Blue Ivy Carter, before appearing on stage and beginning the song along with a choreography.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></li>
<li>At the July 20, 2013 concert in Detroit, Beyoncé covered Sam Cooke's "A Change Is Gonna Come", following the city's file for <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy" title="Bankruptcy">bankruptcy</a>. As Beyoncé performed, the screen behind her displayed photos of Detroit's landmarks and icons including <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">Aretha Franklin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aaliyah" title="Aaliyah">Aaliyah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anita_Baker" title="Anita Baker">Anita Baker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Seger" title="Bob Seger">Bob Seger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kid_Rock" title="Kid Rock">Kid Rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_White_Stripes" title="The White Stripes">The White Stripes</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berry_Gordy,_Jr" title="Berry Gordy, Jr">Berry Gordy, Jr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Louis" title="Joe Louis">Joe Louis</a>. The montage ended with the declaration "Nothing Stops Detroit!".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> A video of Beyoncé's cover of the song at the concert was released through her official YouTube channel on July 30, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></li>
<li>At the August 5, 2013 concert in New York City, Jay-Z appeared on stage unannounced after Beyoncé finished performing "Bow Down". Beyoncé took a seat on stage and Jay-Z performed his song "Tom Ford" (2013). During the end of the performance Beyoncé stood up and provided backing vocals for the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></li>
<li>At the September 20, 2013, concert in Caracas <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> Beyoncé started sing "Irreplaceable" in Spanish.</li>
<li>At the end of Beyoncé's performance at the 2013 Rock in Rio festival, after "Halo", Beyoncé and her dancers performeda choreography on stage to a Brazilian funk song, "Passinho do Volante (Ah Lelek Lek Lek)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></li>
<li>By the time of the first Australian show of the tour on October 22, 2013, "Flaws and All", "I Care", "I Miss You" and "Schoolin' Life" were all cut from the set list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></li>
<li>Beyoncé performed "XO" for the first time during her December 13, 2013 concert in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, the day she unexpectedly released her fifth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9_(album)" title="Beyoncé (album)">Beyoncé</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></li>
<li>On the opening night of the 2014 tour in Glasgow, "Haunted" was used as the opening song, "Drunk in Love" as the second, "If I Were a Boy" as the third, and "Run the World (Girls)" was not performed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></li>
<li>Jay-Z appeared on stage to perform "Drunk in Love" with Beyoncé at all six 2014 shows in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></li>
<li>Jay-Z appeared on stage to perform "Drunk in Love" with Beyoncé on the last show of the tour, in Lisbon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</div>
</div>

<ul>

<li id="cite_note-138"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-138">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The June 28, 2013 concert was a part of <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards_2013#BET_Experience" title="BET Awards 2013">BET Experience 2013</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[133]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-140"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-140">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The July 7, 2013 concert in New Orleans was a part of the <a href="/wiki/Essence_Music_Festival" title="Essence Music Festival">Essence Music Festival</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[134]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-V_Festival-143"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-V_Festival_143-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-V_Festival_143-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The August 17–18, 2013 concerts in Chelmsford and Weston-under-Lizard were a part of the 2013 <a href="/wiki/V_Festival" title="V Festival">V Festival</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[136]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-146"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-146">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The August 31, 2013 concert in Philadelphia was a part of the <a href="/wiki/Budweiser_Made_in_America_Festival" title="Budweiser Made in America Festival">Made in America Music Festival</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[138]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-150"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-150">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The September 13, 2013 concert in Rio de Janeiro was a part of <a href="/wiki/Rock_in_Rio" title="Rock in Rio">Rock in Rio</a> festival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[141]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-152"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-152">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The September 22, 2013 concert in Medellín was held to celebrate the 10th anniversary of <a href="/wiki/W_Radio_(Colombia)" title="W Radio (Colombia)">W Radio</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[142]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-NYC-158"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-NYC_158-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-NYC_158-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The box office score data is representative of both shows at the Barclays Center on December 19 and December 22 respectively.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
